    - Fermented Plant Juice (FPJ) – Extracts nutrients from plants to stimulate growth.
    - Lactic Acid Bacteria (LAB) – Enhances soil health and plant resilience.
    - Water-Soluble Calcium (WCA) – Strengthens plant cell walls.

    - Oriental Herbal Nutrient (OHN) – Protects plants from diseases.
    - Fish Amino Acid (FAA) – Provides essential proteins for plant development.
    Each formula is applied based on the plant’s growth stage to optimize nutrient absorption

commit 98b8c9e3cd50ab6eba94345811c96ca13cd9fadf
Author: Damdoh App <damdoh.org@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu May 22 02:10:55 2025 +0000

    Now, let's go beyond farming and business, i want you to make AI to answers to all these related stake holders also when they want to know about work and preference of each other in this powerful agricultural supply chain linkage platform. The agricultural supply chain involves multiple stakeholders, each playing a crucial role in the production, processing, distribution, and consumption of agricultural products. Here’s a list of key stakeholders:
    - Farmers – The primary producers who cultivate crops and raise livestock.
    - Input Suppliers – Companies providing seeds, fertilizers, pesticides, machinery, and other essential farming inputs.
    - Pre-Harvest Contractors – Service providers assisting farmers with land preparation, planting, irrigation, and pest control.
    - Collection Agents – Individuals or organizations responsible for gathering produce from farms for further processing or distribution.
    - Processors – Businesses that transform raw agricultural products into consumable goods.
    - Traders – Entities involved in buying and selling agricultural products in local and international markets.
    - Retailers – Supermarkets, grocery stores, and other outlets that sell agricultural products to consumers.
    - Exporters – Companies that facilitate the international trade of agricultural goods.
    - Consumers – The end users who purchase and consume agricultural products.
    - Government Agencies – Regulators and facilitators who set policies, provide subsidies, and ensure food safety.
    - Agricultural Cooperatives – Groups of farmers working together to improve market access and share resources.
    - Financial Institutions – Banks and lenders that provide funding and financial support to farmers and agribusinesses.
    - Trade Associations – Organizations advocating for the interests of agricultural stakeholders.
    - Development Personnel – Experts and advisors who assist in agricultural development and sustainability.
